          <img alt="Extensió del valencià al País Valencià.svg" data-file-height="1244" data-file-width="725" height="446" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Extensi%C3%B3_del_valenci%C3%A0_al_Pa%C3%ADs_Valenci%C3%A0.svg/260px-Extensi%C3%B3_del_valenci%C3%A0_al_Pa%C3%ADs_Valenci%C3%A0.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Extensi%C3%B3_del_valenci%C3%A0_al_Pa%C3%ADs_Valenci%C3%A0.svg/390px-Extensi%C3%B3_del_valenci%C3%A0_al_Pa%C3%ADs_Valenci%C3%A0.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Extensi%C3%B3_del_valenci%C3%A0_al_Pa%C3%ADs_Valenci%C3%A0.svg/520px-Extensi%C3%B3_del_valenci%C3%A0_al_Pa%C3%ADs_Valenci%C3%A0.svg.png 2x" width="260"/>

       <tr>
        <td class="noprint selfref" colspan="2" style="text-align:center;background-color:#ddddff;padding:0.3em 0.5em;text-align:left;line-height:1.3;">
         <b>
          This article contains
          <a href="/wiki/International_Phonetic_Alphabet" title="International Phonetic Alphabet">
           IPA
          </a>
          phonetic symbols.
         </b>
         Without proper
         <a href="/wiki/International_Phonetic_Alphabet#Fonts" title="International Phonetic Alphabet">
          rendering support
         </a>
         , you may see
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Replacement_character" title="Replacement character">
          question marks, boxes, or other symbols
         </a>
         instead of
         <a href="/wiki/Unicode" title="Unicode">
          Unicode
         </a>
         characters. For an introductory guide on IPA symbols, see
         <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA" title="Help:IPA">
          Help:IPA
         </a>
         .
        </td>

      <p>
       <b>
        Valencian
       </b>
       (
       <span class="nowrap">
        <span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt">
         <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">
          /
          <span style="border-bottom:1px dotted">
           <span title="'v' in 'vie'">
            v
           </span>
           <span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">
            ə
           </span>
           <span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">
            ˈ
           </span>
           <span title="'l' in 'lie'">
            l
           </span>
           <span title="/ɛ/: 'e' in 'dress'">
            ɛ
           </span>
           <span title="'n' in 'nigh'">
            n
           </span>
           <span title="'s' in 'sigh'">
            s
           </span>
           <span title="/i/: 'y' in 'happy'">
            i
           </span>
           <span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">
            ə
           </span>
           <span title="'n' in 'nigh'">
            n
           </span>
          </span>
          /
         </a>
        </span>
       </span>
       or
       <span class="nowrap">
        <span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt">
         <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">
          /
          <span style="border-bottom:1px dotted">
           <span title="'v' in 'vie'">
            v
           </span>
           <span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">
            ə
           </span>
           <span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">
            ˈ
           </span>
           <span title="'l' in 'lie'">
            l
           </span>
           <span title="/ɛ/: 'e' in 'dress'">
            ɛ
           </span>
           <span title="'n' in 'nigh'">
            n
           </span>
           <span title="/ʃ/: 'sh' in 'shy'">
            ʃ
           </span>
           <span title="/ən/: 'on' in 'button'">
            ən
           </span>
          </span>
          /
         </a>
        </span>
       </span>
       ;
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Endonym" title="Endonym">
        endonym
       </a>
       :
       <i>
        valencià
       </i>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-estatut_5-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-estatut-5">
         [4]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <i>
        llengua valenciana
       </i>
       , or
       <i>
        idioma valencià
       </i>
       ) is a
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Linguistic_variety" title="Linguistic variety">
        linguistic variety
       </a>
       spoken in the
       <a href="/wiki/Valencian_Community" title="Valencian Community">
        Valencian Community
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">
        Spain
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWheeler2006186_6-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWheeler2006186-6">
         [5]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In the Valencian Community, Valencian is the traditional language and is co-official with
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">
        Spanish
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Agreement_7-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Agreement-7">
         [6]
        </a>
       </sup>
       It is considered different from
       <a href="/wiki/Catalan_language" title="Catalan language">
        Catalan
       </a>
       by a slight majority of the people of the Valencian Community (including non-speakers),
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8">
        <a href="#cite_note-8">
         [7]
        </a>
       </sup>
       but this is at odds with the broad academic view, which considers it a dialect of
       <a href="/wiki/Catalan_language" title="Catalan language">
        Catalan
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lavanguardia.mobi_9-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-lavanguardia.mobi-9">
         [8]
        </a>
       </sup>
       A
       <a href="/wiki/Standard_language" title="Standard language">
        standardized
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Variety_(linguistics)#Standard_varieties" title="Variety (linguistics)">
        form
       </a>
       exists, based on the Southern Valencian dialect.
      </p>
      <p>
       Valencian belongs to the Western group of Catalan dialects.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWheeler2006_4-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWheeler2006-4">
         [3]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Under the Valencian
       <a href="/wiki/Statute_of_Autonomy" title="Statute of Autonomy">
        Statute of Autonomy
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Acad%C3%A8mia_Valenciana_de_la_Llengua" title="Acadèmia Valenciana de la Llengua">
        Valencian Academy of the Language
       </a>
       (
       <i>
        Acadèmia Valenciana de la Llengua, AVL
       </i>
       ) has been established as its
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_language_regulators" title="List of language regulators">
        regulator
       </a>
       . The AVL considers
       <i>
        Catalan
       </i>
       and
       <i>
        Valencian
       </i>
       to be simply
       <a href="/wiki/Names_of_the_Catalan_language" title="Names of the Catalan language">
        two names for the same language
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10">
        <a href="#cite_note-10">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Some of the most important works of
       <a href="/wiki/Catalan_literature" title="Catalan literature">
        Valencian literature
       </a>
       experienced a golden age during the
       <a href="/wiki/Late_Middle_Ages" title="Late Middle Ages">
        Late Middle Ages
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Renaissance" title="The Renaissance">
        the Renaissance
       </a>
       . Important works include
       <a href="/wiki/Joanot_Martorell" title="Joanot Martorell">
        Joanot Martorell
       </a>
       's
       <a href="/wiki/Chivalric_romance" title="Chivalric romance">
        chivalric romance
       </a>
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Tirant_lo_Blanch" title="Tirant lo Blanch">
         Tirant lo Blanch
        </a>
       </i>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Ausi%C3%A0s_March" title="Ausiàs March">
        Ausiàs March
       </a>
       's poetry. The first book produced with
       <a href="/wiki/Movable_type" title="Movable type">
        movable type
       </a>
       in the
       <a href="/wiki/Iberian_Peninsula" title="Iberian Peninsula">
        Iberian Peninsula
       </a>
       was printed in the Valencian variety.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11">
        <a href="#cite_note-11">
         [10]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECosta_CarrerasYates20096–7_12-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECosta_CarrerasYates20096–7-12">
         [11]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The earliest recorded
       <a href="/wiki/Chess" title="Chess">
        chess
       </a>
       game with modern rules for moves of the
       <a href="/wiki/Queen_(chess)" title="Queen (chess)">
        queen
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Bishop_(chess)" title="Bishop (chess)">
        bishop
       </a>
       was in the Valencian poem
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Scachs_d%27amor" title="Scachs d'amor">
         Scachs d'amor
        </a>
       </i>
       (1475).
      </p>
      <p>
      </p>

      <p>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Official_status">
        Official status
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Valencian&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Official status">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       The official status of Valencian is regulated by the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spanish_Constitution_of_1978" title="Spanish Constitution of 1978">
        Spanish Constitution
       </a>
       and the Valencian
       <a href="/wiki/Statute_of_Autonomy" title="Statute of Autonomy">
        Statute of Autonomy
       </a>
       , together with the
       <a class="extiw" href="https://ca.wikipedia.org/wiki/Llei_d%27%C3%9As_i_Ensenyament_del_Valenci%C3%A0" title="ca:Llei d'Ús i Ensenyament del Valencià">
        Law of Use and Education of Valencian
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Article 6 of the Valencian Statute of Autonomy sets the legal status of Valencian, providing that:
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-estatuto_13-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-estatuto-13">
         [12]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <ul>
         <li>
          <i>
           The official language of the Valencian Community is Valencian.
          </i>
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14">
           <a href="#cite_note-14">
            [13]
           </a>
          </sup>
         </li>
         <li>
          <i>
           Valencian is official within the Valencian Community, along with Spanish, which is the official language nationwide. Everyone shall have the right to know it and use it, and receive education in Valencian.
          </i>
         </li>
         <li>
          <i>
           No one can be discriminated against by reason of their language
          </i>
          .
         </li>
         <li>
          <i>
           Special protection and respect shall be given to the recuperation of Valencian
          </i>
          .
         </li>
         <li>
          <i>
           The Acadèmia Valenciana de la Llengua shall be the normative institution of the Valencian language
          </i>
          .
         </li>
        </ul>
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <p>
       The
       <a class="extiw" href="https://ca.wikipedia.org/wiki/Llei_d%27%C3%9As_i_Ensenyament_del_Valenci%C3%A0" title="ca:Llei d'Ús i Ensenyament del Valencià">
        Law of Use and Education of Valencian
       </a>
       develops this framework, providing for implementation of a
       <a href="/wiki/Bilingual_education" title="Bilingual education">
        bilingual educational system
       </a>
       , and regulating the use of Valencian in the public administration and judiciary system, where citizens can freely use it when acting before both.
      </p>
      <p>
       Valencian is recognized under the
       <a href="/wiki/European_Charter_for_Regional_or_Minority_Languages" title="European Charter for Regional or Minority Languages">
        European Charter for Regional or Minority Languages
       </a>
       as "Valencian".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15">
        <a href="#cite_note-15">
         [14]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Distribution_and_usage">
        Distribution and usage
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Valencian&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Distribution and usage">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Distribution">
        Distribution
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Valencian&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Distribution">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Valencian is not spoken all over the
       <a href="/wiki/Valencian_Community" title="Valencian Community">
        Valencian Community
       </a>
       . Roughly a quarter of its territory, equivalent to 10% of the population (its inland part and areas in the extreme south as well), is traditionally
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">
        Castilian-speaking
       </a>
       only, whereas Valencian is spoken to varying degrees elsewhere.
      </p>
      <p>
       Additionally, it is also spoken by a reduced number of people in
       <a href="/wiki/Carche" title="Carche">
        Carche
       </a>
       , a rural area in the
       <a href="/wiki/Region_of_Murcia" title="Region of Murcia">
        Region of Murcia
       </a>
       adjoining the Valencian Community; nevertheless Valencian does not have any official recognition in this area. Although the Valencian language was an important part of the history of this zone, nowadays only about 600 people are able to speak Valencian in the area of Carche.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16">
        <a href="#cite_note-16">
         [15]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Knowledge_and_usage">
        Knowledge and usage
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Valencian&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Knowledge and usage">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Coneixement_del_valenci%C3%A0_(domini_promig)-Cens_del_2001.png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="850" data-file-width="600" height="283" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Coneixement_del_valenci%C3%A0_%28domini_promig%29-Cens_del_2001.png/200px-Coneixement_del_valenci%C3%A0_%28domini_promig%29-Cens_del_2001.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Coneixement_del_valenci%C3%A0_%28domini_promig%29-Cens_del_2001.png/300px-Coneixement_del_valenci%C3%A0_%28domini_promig%29-Cens_del_2001.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Coneixement_del_valenci%C3%A0_%28domini_promig%29-Cens_del_2001.png/400px-Coneixement_del_valenci%C3%A0_%28domini_promig%29-Cens_del_2001.png 2x" width="200"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Coneixement_del_valenci%C3%A0_(domini_promig)-Cens_del_2001.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Knowledge of Valencian according to the 2001 census. Note that the light green areas inland and in the southernmost part are not historically Valencian speaking (
         <a class="internal" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/2/24/Coneixement_del_valenci%C3%A0_%28domini_promig%29-Cens_del_2001.png" title="Coneixement del valencià (domini promig)-Cens del 2001.png">
          large
         </a>
         ).
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       In 2010 the
       <a href="/wiki/Generalitat_Valenciana" title="Generalitat Valenciana">
        Generalitat Valenciana
       </a>
       published a study,
       <i>
        Knowledge and Social use of Valencian
       </i>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17">
        <a href="#cite_note-17">
         [16]
        </a>
       </sup>
       which included a survey sampling more than 6,600 people in the provinces of Castellón, Valencia, and Alicante. The survey simply collected the answers of respondents and did not include any testing or verification. The results were:
      </p>
      <p>
       Valencian was the language "
       <i>
        always, generally, or most commonly used
       </i>
       ":
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        at home: 31.6%
       </li>
       <li>
        with friends: 28.0%
       </li>
       <li>
        in internal business relations: 24.7%
       </li>
      </ul>
      <p>
       For ability:
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        48.5% answered they speak Valencian "perfectly" or "quite well" (54.3% in the Valencian-speaking areas and 10% in the Castilian-speaking areas)
       </li>
       <li>
        26.2% answered they write Valencian "perfectly" or "quite well" (29.5% in the Valencian-speaking areas and 5.8% in the Castilian-speaking areas)
       </li>
      </ul>
      <p>
       The survey shows that, although Valencian is still the common language in many areas in the Valencian Community, where slightly more than half of the Valencian population are able to speak it, most Valencians do not usually speak in Valencian in their social relations. The statistics hide the fact that in the areas where the language is still strong, most people use Valencian in preference to Castilian in all everyday situations.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2017)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Moreover, according to a survey in 2008, there is a downward trend in everyday Valencian users. The lowest numbers are in the major cities of
       <a href="/wiki/Valencia" title="Valencia">
        Valencia
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Alicante" title="Alicante">
        Alicante
       </a>
       , where the percentage of everyday speakers is in single figures. All in all, in the 1993–2006 period, the number of speakers fell by 10 per cent.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18">
        <a href="#cite_note-18">
         [17]
        </a>
       </sup>
       One of the factors cited is the
       <a href="/wiki/Immigration_to_Spain" title="Immigration to Spain">
        increase in the numbers of immigrants from other countries
       </a>
       , who tend to favour using Spanish over local languages; accordingly, the number of residents who claim no understanding of Valencian sharply increased. One curiosity in the heartlands mentioned above, is that most of the children of immigrants go to public school and are therefore taught in Valencian and are far more comfortable speaking this with their friends. However, some children of Valencian speakers go to private schools run by the church where the curriculum is in Castilian and consequently this becomes their preferred language.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Features_of_Valencian">
        Features of Valencian
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Valencian&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Features of Valencian">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       Note that this is a list of features of the main forms of Valencian as a group of dialectal varieties that differ from those of other Catalan dialects, particularly from the Central variety of the language. For more general information on the features of Valencian, see
       <a href="/wiki/Catalan_language" title="Catalan language">
        Catalan language
       </a>
       . Note also that there is a great deal of variety within the Valencian Community, and by no means do the features below apply to every local version.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Phonology">
        Phonology
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Valencian&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Phonology">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Catalan_phonology" title="Catalan phonology">
        Catalan phonology
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       <span class="plainlinks selfreference noprint">
        For assistance with IPA transcriptions of Valencian for Wikipedia articles, see
        <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Catalan" title="Help:IPA/Catalan">
         Help:IPA/Catalan
        </a>
        .
       </span>
      </div>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Vowels">
        Vowels
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>

       </span>
      </h4>

          .
          <span class="hide-when-compact">
           Please help
           <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Valencian&amp;action=edit">
            improve this article
           </a>
           by
           <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">
            adding citations to reliable sources
           </a>
           . Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.
          </span>
          <small>
           <i>
            (April 2017)
           </i>
          </small>
          <small class="hide-when-compact">
           <i>
            (
            <a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">
             Learn how and when to remove this template message
            </a>
            )
           </i>
          </small>
         </div>
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>

         </a>

         </a>
        </sup>
       </caption>
       <tr>
        <th>

         </a>
        </th>
       </tr>
       <tr align="center">
        <th>

         </a>
        </th>
        <td>
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">

          </a>
         </span>
        </td>
        <td>
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          <a href="/wiki/Close_back_rounded_vowel" title="Close back rounded vowel">

          </a>
         </span>
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr align="center">
        <th>

         </a>
        </th>
        <td>
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">

          </a>
         </span>
        </td>
        <td>
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          <a href="/wiki/Close-mid_back_rounded_vowel" title="Close-mid back rounded vowel">
           o
          </a>
         </span>
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr align="center">

         </a>
         /
         <br/>

          Open
         </a>
        </th>
        <td>
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          <a href="/wiki/Near-open_front_unrounded_vowel" title="Near-open front unrounded vowel">
           ɛ
          </a>
         </span>
        </td>
        <td>
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          <a href="/wiki/Open_back_rounded_vowel" title="Open back rounded vowel">
           ɔ
          </a>
         </span>
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr align="center">
        <td colspan="3" style="text-align:center;">
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          <a href="/wiki/Near-open_central_unrounded_vowel" title="Near-open central unrounded vowel">
           a
          </a>
         </span>
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Valencian has a system of seven stressed vowels
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /i, u, e, o, ɛ, ɔ, a/
        </span>
        .
        <ul>
         <li>
          The vowels
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           /i/
          </span>
          (i.e.
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           [i̽]
          </span>
          ) and
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           /u/
          </span>
          (
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           [u̽]
          </span>
          ) are more open and centralised than in Castilian.
          <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
           [
           <i>
            <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
             <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2017)">
              citation needed
             </span>
            </a>
           </i>
           ]
          </sup>
         </li>
         <li>
          The vowel
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           /e/
          </span>
          is retracted and
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           /o/
          </span>
          is advanced both in stressed and unstressed syllables.
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           /e/
          </span>
          and
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           /o/
          </span>
          can be realised as mid vowels in some cases. This occurs more often with
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           /o/
          </span>
          .
          <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
           [
           <i>
            <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
             <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2017)">
              citation needed
             </span>
            </a>
           </i>
           ]
          </sup>
         </li>
         <li>
          The so-called "
          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mid-open_vowel" title="Mid-open vowel">
           open vowels
          </a>
          " (
          <i>
           vocals obertes
          </i>
          ),
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           /ɛ/
          </span>
          and
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           /ɔ/
          </span>
          , are generally as low as
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           /a/
          </span>
          in most Valencian dialects. The phonetic realisations of
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           /ɛ/
          </span>
          approaches
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           [
           <a href="/wiki/Near-open_front_unrounded_vowel" title="Near-open front unrounded vowel">
            æ
           </a>
           ]
          </span>
          (as in American English
          <i>
           b
           <b>
            a
           </b>
           d
          </i>
          ) and
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           /ɔ/
          </span>
          is as open as
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           [
           <a href="/wiki/Open_back_rounded_vowel" title="Open back rounded vowel">
            ɒ
           </a>
           ]
          </span>
          (as in traditional
          <a href="/wiki/Received_Pronunciation" title="Received Pronunciation">
           RP
          </a>
          <i>
           d
           <b>
            o
           </b>
           g
          </i>
          ). This feature is also found in
          <a href="/wiki/Balearic_dialect" title="Balearic dialect">
           Balearic
          </a>
          .
          <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
           [
           <i>
            <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
             <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2017)">
              citation needed
             </span>
            </a>
           </i>
           ]
          </sup>
          <ul>
           <li>
            <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
             /ɛ/
            </span>
            is slightly more open and centralised before liquids
            <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
             /l, r/
            </span>
            and in monosyllabics.
            <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
             [
             <i>
              <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
               <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2017)">
                citation needed
               </span>
              </a>
             </i>
             ]
            </sup>
           </li>
           <li>
            <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
             /ɔ/
            </span>
            is most often a back vowel. In some dialects (including Balearic) it can be unrounded like in American English.
            <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
             [
             <i>
              <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
               <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2017)">
                citation needed
               </span>
              </a>
             </i>
             ]
            </sup>
           </li>
          </ul>
         </li>
         <li>
          The vowel
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           /a/
          </span>
          is slightly more fronted and closed than in Central Catalan (but less fronted and closed than in Majorcan). The precise phonetic realsation of the vowel
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           /a/
          </span>
          in Valencian is
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           [ɐ ~ ä]
          </span>
          , this vowel is subject to assimilation in many instances.
          <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
           [
           <i>
            <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
             <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2017)">
              citation needed
             </span>
            </a>
           </i>
           ]
          </sup>
          <ul>
           <li>
            <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
             /a/
            </span>
            can be retracted in contact with velar consonants, and fronted in contact with palatals.
            <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
             [
             <i>
              <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
               <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2017)">
                citation needed
               </span>
              </a>
             </i>
             ]
            </sup>
           </li>
           <li>
            Final unstressed
            <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
             /a/
            </span>
            may be
            <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
             [ɐ ~ ä]
            </span>
            , depending on the preceding sounds and/or dialect, e.g.
            <i>
             taula
            </i>
            <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
             [ˈtɑ̟wɫɐ ~ ˈtɑ̟wɫä]
            </span>
            'table'.
            <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
             [
             <i>
              <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
               <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2017)">
                citation needed
               </span>
              </a>
             </i>
             ]
            </sup>
           </li>
          </ul>
         </li>
         <li>
          All vowels are phonetically nasalised between nasal consonants or when preceding a syllable-final nasal.
         </li>
         <li>
          Vowels can be lengthened in some contexts.
          <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
           [
           <i>
            <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
             <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2017)">
              citation needed
             </span>
            </a>
           </i>
           ]
          </sup>
         </li>
        </ul>
       </li>
       <li>
        While unstressed vowels are more stable than in Eastern Catalan dialects, there are many cases where they merge
        <ul>
         <li>
          In some Valencian subvarieties, unstressed
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           /o/
          </span>
          and
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           /ɔ/
          </span>
          are realised as
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           [ʊ]
          </span>
          before labial consonants (e.g.
          <i>
           c
           <b>
            o
           </b>
           berts
          </i>
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           [kʊˈbæ̈ɾ(t)s]
          </span>
          'cutlery'), before a stressed syllable with a high vowel (e.g.
          <i>
           s
           <b>
            o
           </b>
           spira
          </i>
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           [sʊsˈpiɾä]
          </span>
          or
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           [sʊsˈpiɾæ̈]
          </span>
          'he/she sighs'), in contact with palatal consonants (e.g.
          <i>
           J
           <b>
            o
           </b>
           sep
          </i>
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           [dʒʊˈzæp]
          </span>
          'Joseph') and in monosyllabic clitics (e.g.
          <i>
           m
           <b>
            o
           </b>
           n
          </i>
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           [mʊn]
          </span>
          'my') (note also in many colloquial speeches initial unstressed
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           /o ~ ɔ/
          </span>
          are often reduced to
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           [ɑ̈w]
          </span>
          or
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           [äw]
          </span>
          (also
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           [ʊ]
          </span>
          in fewer cases), such as
          <i>
           <b>
            o
           </b>
           lor
          </i>
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           [ɑ̈wˈɫo̞ɾ]
          </span>
          ) 'smell (n)'). Similarly, unstressed
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           /e/
          </span>
          , and
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           /ɛ/
          </span>
          are realised as
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           [a]
          </span>
          in contact with palatals, approximants or before certain sounds (e.g.
          <i>
           <b>
            e
           </b>
           ixam
          </i>
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           [ajˈʃam]
          </span>
          'swarm',
          <i>
           cl
           <b>
            e
           </b>
           vill
          </i>
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           [kɫaˈʋiʎ]
          </span>
          'crevice',
          <i>
           t
           <b>
            e
           </b>
           rròs
          </i>
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           [taˈrɒ̈s]
          </span>
          'clod',) and (
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           [ɑ̈]
          </span>
          or
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           [ä]
          </span>
          )) in fewer cases near velars (e.g.
          <i>
           <b>
            e
           </b>
           nclusa
          </i>
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           [ɑ̈ŋˈkɫuzɑ̈]
          </span>
          or
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           [ɑ̈ŋˈkɫuzæ̈]
          </span>
          'anvil').
          <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
           [
           <i>
            <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
             <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2017)">
              citation needed
             </span>
            </a>
           </i>
           ]
          </sup>
          Likewise, unstressed
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           /e ~ ɛ/
          </span>
          merges with
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           /i/
          </span>
          (
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           [ɪ]
          </span>
          ) in contact with
          <a href="/wiki/Alveolo-palatal_consonant" title="Alveolo-palatal consonant">
           palatal consonants
          </a>
          (e.g.
          <i>
           g
           <b>
            e
           </b>
           noll
          </i>
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           [dʒɪˈno̞ʎ]
          </span>
          'knee'), and especially in lexical derivation with the suffix -
          <i>
           ix
           <b>
            e
           </b>
           ment
          </i>
          (e.g.
          <i>
           coneix
           <b>
            e
           </b>
           ment
          </i>
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           [konejʃɪˈment]
          </span>
          'knowledge'). In the Standard all these reductions are accepted (
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           /e, ɛ/
          </span>
          →
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           [ɪ]
          </span>
          is only accepted in words with the suffix
          <i>
           -ixement
          </i>
          ).
          <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
           [
           <i>
            <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
             <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2017)">
              citation needed
             </span>
            </a>
           </i>
           ]
          </sup>
         </li>
         <li>
          Many Valencian subdialects, especially Southern Valencian, feature some sort of
          <a href="/wiki/Vowel_harmony" title="Vowel harmony">
           vowel harmony
          </a>
          (
          <i>
           harmonia vocàlica
          </i>
          ). This process is normally progressive (i.e. preceding vowels affect those pronounced afterwards) over the last unstressed vowel of a word; e.g.
          <i>
           h
           <b>
            o
           </b>
           r
           <b>
            a
           </b>
          </i>
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           /ˈɔɾa/
          </span>
          &gt;
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           [ˈɒɾɒ̈]
          </span>
          'hour'. However, there are cases where regressive metaphony occurs over pretonic vowels; e.g.
          <i>
           t
           <b>
            o
           </b>
           v
           <b>
            a
           </b>
           ll
           <b>
            o
           </b>
           l
           <b>
            a
           </b>
          </i>
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           /tovaˈʎɔla/
          </span>
          &gt;
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           [tɒ̈ʋɒ̈ˈʎɒɫɒ̈]
          </span>
          'towel',
          <i>
           <b>
            a
           </b>
           f
           <b>
            e
           </b>
           ct
           <b>
            a
           </b>
          </i>
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           /aˈfɛkta/
          </span>
          &gt;
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           [æ̈ˈfæktæ̈]
          </span>
          'affects'. Vowel harmony differs greatly from dialect to dialect, while many subvarieties alternate
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           [æ̈]
          </span>
          and
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           [ɒ̈]
          </span>
          , according to the previous stressed vowel (e.g.
          <i>
           terra
          </i>
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           [ˈtæræ̈]
          </span>
          'Earth, land' and
          <i>
           dona
          </i>
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           [ˈdɒnɒ̈]
          </span>
          'woman'); others will favor just one realisation (either
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           [æ̈]
          </span>
          in all, or some, instances; or
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           [ɒ̈]
          </span>
          ), thus,
          <i>
           terra
          </i>
          and
          <i>
           dona
          </i>
          can be pronounced
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           [ˈtæræ̈]
          </span>
          and
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           [ˈdɒnæ̈]
          </span>
          (by those who favour
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           [æ̈]
          </span>
          ) or
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           [ˈtærɒ̈]
          </span>
          and
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           [ˈdɒnɒ̈]
          </span>
          (by those who favour
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           [ɒ̈]
          </span>
          ).
          <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
           [
           <i>
            <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
             <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2017)">
              citation needed
             </span>
            </a>
           </i>
           ]
          </sup>
          <ul>
           <li>
            In a wider sense, vowel harmony can occur in further instances, due to different processes involving palatalisation, velarisarion and labialisation.
            <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
             [
             <i>
              <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
               <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2017)">
                citation needed
               </span>
              </a>
             </i>
             ]
            </sup>
           </li>
          </ul>
         </li>
         <li>
          An epethentic vowel (usually pronounced
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           [ɐ]
          </span>
          or
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           [ɜ]
          </span>
          , but transcribed here as
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           [ə]
          </span>
          ) may be inserted in some environments in the coda in some accents:
          <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
           [
           <i>
            <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
             <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2017)">
              citation needed
             </span>
            </a>
           </i>
           ]
          </sup>
          <ul>
           <li>
            <i>
             Eh tu! Vine ací
            </i>
            <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
             [ˈeː ˈtuːə̯ | ˈvine äˈsiːə̯]
            </span>
            "Hey you! Come here".
           </li>
          </ul>
         </li>
        </ul>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <p>
       In the table below, the vowels are transcribed in a very narrow transcription. In the rest of the article, the symbols
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [a̠, ɑ̝, ɑ̝̈, ɒ̝̈, e̠, ɪ̞, i̞, ɒ̝, o̟, ʊ̞, u̞]
       </span>
       are written
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [a, ɑ, ɑ̈, ɒ̈, e, ɪ, i, ɒ, o, ʊ, u]
       </span>
       for the sake of simplicity.
      </p>

         </i>
