         </span>
        </td>
        <td style="border-right: 0;" width="25px">
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Voiceless_apico-alveolar_sibilant" title="Voiceless apico-alveolar sibilant">
           s
          </a>
         </span>
        </td>
        <td style="border-left: 0;" width="25px">
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Voiced_apico-alveolar_sibilant" title="Voiced apico-alveolar sibilant">
           z
          </a>
         </span>
        </td>
        <td style="border-right: 0;" width="25px">
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          <a href="/wiki/Voiceless_alveolo-palatal_fricative" title="Voiceless alveolo-palatal fricative">
           ʃ
          </a>
         </span>
        </td>
        <td style="border-left: 0;" width="25px">
         (
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          <a href="/wiki/Voiced_alveolo-palatal_fricative" title="Voiced alveolo-palatal fricative">
           ʒ
          </a>
         </span>
         )
        </td>
        <td colspan="2">
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <th>
         <a href="/wiki/Approximant_consonant" title="Approximant consonant">
          Approximant
         </a>
        </th>
        <td colspan="2">
        </td>
        <td colspan="2">
        </td>
        <td colspan="2">
        </td>
        <td style="border-right: 0;">
        </td>
        <td style="border-left: 0;">
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          <a href="/wiki/Palatal_approximant#Palatal" title="Palatal approximant">
           j
          </a>
         </span>
        </td>
        <td style="border-right: 0;">
        </td>
        <td style="border-left: 0;">
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          <a href="/wiki/Voiced_labio-velar_approximant" title="Voiced labio-velar approximant">
           w
          </a>
         </span>
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <th>
         <a href="/wiki/Lateral_consonant" title="Lateral consonant">
          Lateral
         </a>
        </th>
        <td colspan="2">
        </td>
        <td colspan="2">
        </td>
        <td style="border-right: 0;">
        </td>
        <td style="border-left: 0;">
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alveolar_lateral_approximant" title="Alveolar lateral approximant">
           l
          </a>
         </span>
        </td>
        <td style="border-right: 0;">
        </td>
        <td style="border-left: 0;">
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          <a href="/wiki/Palatal_lateral_approximant" title="Palatal lateral approximant">
           ʎ
          </a>
         </span>
        </td>
        <td colspan="2">
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <th>
         <a href="/wiki/Flap_consonant" title="Flap consonant">
          Flap
         </a>
        </th>
        <td colspan="2">
        </td>
        <td colspan="2">
        </td>
        <td style="border-right: 0;">
        </td>
        <td style="border-left: 0;">
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alveolar_flap" title="Alveolar flap">
           ɾ
          </a>
         </span>
        </td>
        <td colspan="2">
        </td>
        <td colspan="2">
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <th>
         <a href="/wiki/Trill_consonant" title="Trill consonant">
          Trill
         </a>
        </th>
        <td colspan="2">
        </td>
        <td colspan="2">
        </td>
        <td style="border-right: 0;">
        </td>
        <td style="border-left: 0;">
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alveolar_trill" title="Alveolar trill">
           r
          </a>
         </span>
        </td>
        <td colspan="2">
        </td>
        <td colspan="2">
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <ul>
       <li>
        The
        <a href="/wiki/Voice_(phonetics)" title="Voice (phonetics)">
         voiced
        </a>
        stops
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /d, ɡ/
        </span>
        are
        <a href="/wiki/Lenition" title="Lenition">
         lenited
        </a>
        to approximants
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         [
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dental_approximant" title="Dental approximant">
           ð
          </a>
         </span>
         ,
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          <a href="/wiki/Voiced_velar_approximant" title="Voiced velar approximant">
           ɣ
          </a>
         </span>
         ]
        </span>
        after a
        <a href="/wiki/Continuant" title="Continuant">
         continuant
        </a>
        , i.e. a vowel or any type of consonant other than a
        <a href="/wiki/Stop_consonant" title="Stop consonant">
         stop
        </a>
        or
        <a href="/wiki/Nasal_consonant" title="Nasal consonant">
         nasal
        </a>
        (exceptions include
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /d/
        </span>
        after
        <a href="/wiki/Lateral_consonant" title="Lateral consonant">
         lateral consonants
        </a>
        ). These sounds are realised as voiceless plosives in the coda in standard Valencian.
        <ul>
         <li>
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           /b/
          </span>
          can also be lenited in betacist dialects.
         </li>
         <li>
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           /d/
          </span>
          is often elided between vowels following a stressed syllable (found notably in feminine participles); e.g.
          <i>
           fideuà
          </i>
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           [fiðeˈwɑ̈ː]
          </span>
          ( &lt;
          <i>
           fideua
           <b>
            d
           </b>
           a
          </i>
          ) '
          <a href="/wiki/Fideu%C3%A0" title="Fideuà">
           fideuà
          </a>
          '.
         </li>
         <li>
          Unlike other Catalan dialects, the clusters
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           /bl/
          </span>
          and
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           /ɡl/
          </span>
          never geminate or fortify in intervocalic position (e.g.
          <i>
           po
           <b>
            b
           </b>
           le
          </i>
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           [ˈpɒbɫe]
          </span>
          'village').
         </li>
        </ul>
       </li>
       <li>
        The velar stops
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /k/
        </span>
        ,
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /ɡ/
        </span>
        are fronted to pre-velar position before
        <a href="/wiki/Front_vowel" title="Front vowel">
         front vowels
        </a>
        .
       </li>
       <li>
        Valencian has preserved in most of its subvarieties the mediaeval
        <a href="/wiki/Voiced_alveolo-palatal_affricate" title="Voiced alveolo-palatal affricate">
         voiced alveolo-palatal affricate
        </a>
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /
         <a href="/wiki/Voiced_alveolo-palatal_affricate" title="Voiced alveolo-palatal affricate">
          dʒ
         </a>
         /
        </span>
        (similar to the
        <i>
         j
        </i>
        in English "jeep") in contexts where other modern dialects have developed
        <a href="/wiki/Fricative_consonant" title="Fricative consonant">
         fricative consonants
        </a>
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /ʒ/
        </span>
        (like the
        <i>
         si
        </i>
        in English "vision"); this is a feature shared with modern Ribagorçan. Nonetheless, the fricative
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         [
         <a href="/wiki/Voiced_alveolo-palatal_fricative" title="Voiced alveolo-palatal fricative">
          ʒ
         </a>
         ]
        </span>
        may appear as a voiced
        <a href="/wiki/Allophone" title="Allophone">
         allophone
        </a>
        of
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /ʃ/
        </span>
        before vowels and voiced consonants; e.g.
        <i>
         pe
         <b>
          ix
         </b>
         al forn
        </i>
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         [ˈpejʒ ɑ̈ɫ ˈfo̞ɾn]
        </span>
        'oven fish' (literally 'fish to the oven').
       </li>
       <li>
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /v/
        </span>
        occurs in Balearic,
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECarbonellLlisterri199253_25-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECarbonellLlisterri199253-25">
          [24]
         </a>
        </sup>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alguerese" title="Alguerese">
         Alguerese
        </a>
        , standard Valencian and some areas in southern Catalonia.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVeny200751_26-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVeny200751-26">
          [25]
         </a>
        </sup>
        It has
        <a href="/wiki/Betacism" title="Betacism">
         merged
        </a>
        with
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /b/
        </span>
        <a href="/wiki/Catalan_language#Consonants" title="Catalan language">
         elsewhere
        </a>
        .
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27">
         <a href="#cite_note-27">
          [26]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        Deaffrication of
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /dz/
        </span>
        in verbs ending in -
        <i>
         itzar
        </i>
        ; e.g.
        <i>
         anali
         <b>
          tz
         </b>
         ar
        </i>
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         [ɑ̈nɑ̈ɫiˈzɑ̈ɾ]
        </span>
        'to analise'.
       </li>
       <li>
        Most subvarieties of Valencian preserve final stops in clusters (e.g.
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /mp/, /nt/, /nk/ ([ŋk])
        </span>
        , and
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /lt/
        </span>
        ):
        <i>
         ca
         <b>
          mp
         </b>
        </i>
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         [kɑ̈mp]
        </span>
        (a feature shared with modern
        <a href="/wiki/Balearic_dialect" title="Balearic dialect">
         Balearic
        </a>
        ). Dialectally, all final clusters can be simplified.
       </li>
       <li>
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /l/
        </span>
        is normally
        <a href="/wiki/Velarization" title="Velarization">
         velarised
        </a>
        (
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         [ɫ]
        </span>
        ), save for some dialects.
        <ul>
         <li>
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           /l/
          </span>
          is generally
          <a href="/wiki/Elision" title="Elision">
           dropped
          </a>
          in the word
          <i>
           altre
          </i>
          (
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           [ˈɑ̈tɾe]
          </span>
          'other'), as well as in derived terms.
          <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
           [
           <i>
            <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
             <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2017)">
              citation needed
             </span>
            </a>
           </i>
           ]
          </sup>
         </li>
        </ul>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Morphology">
        Morphology
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Valencian&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Morphology">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <ul>
       <li>
        The present first-person singular of verbs differs from Central Catalan; e.g. -
        <i>
         ar
        </i>
        infinitive:
        <i>
         parlar
        </i>
        'to speak' gives
        <i>
         parle
        </i>
        'I speak' as opposed to
        <i>
         parlo
        </i>
        , -
        <i>
         re
        </i>
        infinitive:
        <i>
         batre
        </i>
        'to beat' gives
        <i>
         bat
        </i>
        'I beat' as opposed to
        <i>
         bato
        </i>
        , -
        <i>
         er
        </i>
        infinitive:
        <i>
         témer
        </i>
        'to fear' give
        <i>
         tem
        </i>
        'I fear' as opposed to
        <i>
         temo
        </i>
        , and -
        <i>
         ir
        </i>
        infinitive:
        <i>
         sentir
        </i>
        'to feel' gives
        <i>
         sent
        </i>
        (pronounced
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         [ˈseŋk]
        </span>
        in colloquial Valencian) 'I feel' as opposed to
        <i>
         sento
        </i>
        (all those forms without final -
        <i>
         o
        </i>
        are more akin to mediaeval Catalan and contemporary Balearic Catalan), and inchoative -
        <i>
         ir
        </i>
        verbs:
        <i>
         patir
        </i>
        'to suffer' gives
        <i>
         patisc
        </i>
        or
        <i>
         patesc
        </i>
        ('I suffer') as opposed to
        <i>
         pateixo
        </i>
        .
       </li>
       <li>
        Present subjunctive is more akin to mediaeval Catalan and Spanish; -
        <i>
         ar
        </i>
        infinitives end ⟨e⟩, -
        <i>
         re
        </i>
        , -
        <i>
         er
        </i>
        and -
        <i>
         ir
        </i>
        verbs end in ⟨a⟩ (in contemporary Central Catalan present subjunctive ends in ⟨i⟩).
       </li>
       <li>
        An exclusive feature of Valencian is the
        <a href="/wiki/Subjunctive_mood" title="Subjunctive mood">
         subjunctive
        </a>
        imperfect morpheme -
        <i>
         ra
        </i>
        :
        <i>
         que ell vinguera
        </i>
        ('that he might come').
       </li>
       <li>
        Valencian has -
        <i>
         i
        </i>
        - as theme vowel for inchoative verbs of the third conjugation; e.g.
        <i>
         servix
        </i>
        ('s/he serves'), like North-Western Catalan. Although, again, this cannot be generalized since there are Valencian subdialects that utilize -
        <i>
         ei
        </i>
        -, e.g.
        <i>
         serveix
        </i>
        .
       </li>
       <li>
        In Valencian the simple past tense (e.g.
        <i>
         cantà
        </i>
        'he sang') is more frequently used in speech than in Central Catalan, where the periphrastic past (e.g.
        <i>
         va cantar
        </i>
        'he sang') is prevailing and the simple past mostly appears in written language. The same, however, may be said of the Balearic dialects.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-badia_28-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-badia-28">
          [27]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        The second-person singular of the present tense of the verb
        <i>
         ser
        </i>
        ('to be'),
        <i>
         ets
        </i>
        ('you are'), has been replaced by
        <i>
         eres
        </i>
        in colloquial speech.
       </li>
      </ul>
      <dl>
       <dt>
        Clitics
       </dt>
      </dl>
      <ul>
       <li>
        In general, use of modern forms of the determinate article (
        <i>
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/el#Catalan" title="wikt:el">
          el
         </a>
         ,
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/els#Catalan" title="wikt:els">
          els
         </a>
        </i>
        'the') and the third-person unstressed object pronouns (
        <i>
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/el#Catalan" title="wikt:el">
          el
         </a>
         ,
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/els#Catalan" title="wikt:els">
          els
         </a>
        </i>
        'him, them'), though some subdialects (for instance the one spoken in
        <a href="/wiki/Vinar%C3%B2s" title="Vinaròs">
         Vinaròs
        </a>
        area) preserve etymological forms
        <i>
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/lo#Catalan" title="wikt:lo">
          lo
         </a>
        </i>
        ,
        <i>
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/los#Catalan" title="wikt:los">
          los
         </a>
        </i>
        as in
        <a href="/wiki/Lleida" title="Lleida">
         Lleida
        </a>
        . For the other unstressed object pronouns, etymological old forms (
        <i>
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/me#Catalan" title="wikt:me">
          me
         </a>
        </i>
        ,
        <i>
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/te#Catalan" title="wikt:te">
          te
         </a>
        </i>
        ,
        <i>
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/se#Catalan" title="wikt:se">
          se
         </a>
        </i>
        ,
        <i>
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/ne#Catalan" title="wikt:ne">
          ne
         </a>
        </i>
        ,
        <i>
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/mos#Catalan" title="wikt:mos">
          mos
         </a>
        </i>
        ,
        <i>
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/vos#Catalan" title="wikt:vos">
          vos
         </a>
        </i>
        ...) can be found, depending on places, in conjunction with the more modern reinforced ones (
        <i>
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/em#Catalan" title="wikt:em">
          em
         </a>
        </i>
        ,
        <i>
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/et#Catalan" title="wikt:et">
          et
         </a>
        </i>
        ,
        <i>
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/es#Catalan" title="wikt:es">
          es
         </a>
        </i>
        ,
        <i>
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/en#Catalan" title="wikt:en">
          en
         </a>
        </i>
        ,
        <i>
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/ens#Catalan" title="wikt:ens">
          ens
         </a>
        </i>
        ,
        <i>
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/us#Catalan" title="wikt:us">
          us
         </a>
        </i>
        ...).
        <ul>
         <li>
          Several variations for
          <i>
           <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/nosaltres#Catalan" title="wikt:nosaltres">
            nosaltres
           </a>
          </i>
          ,
          <i>
           <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/vosaltres#Catalan" title="wikt:vosaltres">
            vosaltres
           </a>
          </i>
          ('we, you'):
          <i>
           mosatros, moatros, natros; vosatros, voatros, vatros
          </i>
          ; also for the weak form
          <i>
           mos
          </i>
          /-
          <i>
           mos
          </i>
          instead of standard
          <i>
           ens
          </i>
          /
          <i>
           -nos
          </i>
          ('us').
         </li>
        </ul>
       </li>
       <li>
        The adverbial pronoun
        <i>
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/hi#Catalan" title="wikt:hi">
          hi
         </a>
        </i>
        ('there') is almost never used in speech and is replaced by other pronouns. The adverbial pronoun
        <i>
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/en" title="wikt:en">
          en
         </a>
        </i>
        ('him/her/them/it') is used less than in Catalonia and the Balearic Islands.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-badia_28-1">
         <a href="#cite_note-badia-28">
          [27]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Catalan_personal_pronouns" title="Catalan personal pronouns">
         Combined weak clitics
        </a>
        with
        <i>
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/li#Catalan" title="wikt:li">
          li
         </a>
        </i>
        ('him/her/it') preserve the
        <i>
         li
        </i>
        , whereas in Central Catalan it is replaced by
        <i>
         hi
        </i>
        . For example, the combination
        <i>
         li
        </i>
        +
        <i>
         el
        </i>
        gives
        <i>
         li'l
        </i>
        in Valencian (
        <i>
         l'hi
        </i>
        in Central Catalan).
       </li>
       <li>
        The weak pronoun
        <i>
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/ho#Catalan" title="wikt:ho">
          ho
         </a>
        </i>
        ('it') is pronounced as
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         [ew]
        </span>
        more often than in other dialects, especially when coming after another pronoun (e.g.
        <i>
         m'ho dóna
        </i>
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         [mew ˈðona]
        </span>
        ,
        <i>
         dóna-m'ho
        </i>
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         [ˈdonamew]
        </span>
        's/he gives it to me'). However, when preceding a verb on its own it is pronounced as
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         [u]
        </span>
        :
        <i>
         ho dóna
        </i>
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         [u ˈðona]
        </span>
        's/he gives it'. Moreover, after a verb ending in a vowel it is pronounced as
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         [w]
        </span>
        (e.g.
        <i>
         dóna-ho
        </i>
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         [ˈdonaw]
        </span>
        'you give it'); while, when following a verb ending with a consonant it is pronounced as
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         [o]
        </span>
        :
        <i>
         donar-ho
        </i>
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         [doˈnaɾo]
        </span>
        'to give it'.
       </li>
       <li>
        The personal pronoun
        <i>
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/jo#Catalan" title="wikt:jo">
          jo
         </a>
        </i>
        ('I') and the adverb
        <i>
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/ja#Catalan" title="wikt:ja">
          ja
         </a>
        </i>
        ('already') are not pronounced according to the spelling, but to the etymology (
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         [ˈjɒ]
        </span>
        and
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         [ˈja]
        </span>
        , instead of
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /ˈ(d)ʒɔ/
        </span>
        and
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /ˈ(d)ʒa/
        </span>
        ). Similar pronunciations can be heard in North-Western Catalan and Ibizan.
       </li>
       <li>
        The preposition
        <i>
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/amb#Catalan" title="wikt:amb">
          amb
         </a>
        </i>
        ('with') merges with
        <i>
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/en#Catalan" title="wikt:en">
          en
         </a>
        </i>
        ('in') in most Valencian subdialects.
       </li>
       <li>
        Valencian preserves the mediaeval system of demonstratives with three different levels of demonstrative precision (
        <i>
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/este#Catalan" title="wikt:este">
          este
         </a>
        </i>
        or
        <i>
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/aquest#Catalan" title="wikt:aquest">
          aquest
         </a>
        </i>
        /
        <i>
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/a%C3%A7%C3%B2#Catalan" title="wikt:açò">
          açò
         </a>
        </i>
        /
        <i>
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/ac%C3%AD#Catalan" title="wikt:ací">
          ací
         </a>
        </i>
        ,
        <i>
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/eixe#Catalan" title="wikt:eixe">
          eixe
         </a>
        </i>
        or
        <i>
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/aqueix#Catalan" title="wikt:aqueix">
          aqueix
         </a>
        </i>
        /
        <i>
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/aix%C3%B2#Catalan" title="wikt:això">
          això
         </a>
        </i>
        /
        <i>
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/aqu%C3%AD#Catalan" title="wikt:aquí">
          ahí
         </a>
        </i>
        ,
        <i>
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/aquell#Catalan" title="wikt:aquell">
          aquell
         </a>
        </i>
        /
        <i>
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/all%C3%B2#Catalan" title="wikt:allò">
          allò
         </a>
        </i>
        /
        <i>
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/all%C3%AD#Catalan" title="wikt:allí">
          allí
         </a>
        </i>
        or
        <i>
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/all%C3%A0#Catalan" title="wikt:allà">
          allà
         </a>
        </i>
        , where "aquest" and "aqueix" are almost never used) (feature shared with modern Ribagorçan and Tortosí).
       </li>
      </ul>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Vocabulary">
        Vocabulary
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Valencian&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Vocabulary">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Valencian vocuabulary contains words both restricted to the Valencian-speaking domain, as well as words shared with other Catalan varieties, especially with
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Northwestern_Catalan" title="Northwestern Catalan">
        Northwestern ones
       </a>
       . Words are rarely spread evenly over the Valencian community, but are usually contained to parts of it, or spread out into other dialectal areas. Examples include
       <i>
        hui
       </i>
       'today' (found in all of Valencia except transitional dialects, in Northern dialects
       <i>
        avui
       </i>
       ) and
       <i>
        espill
       </i>
       'mirror' (shared with Northwestern dialects, Central Catalan
       <i>
        mirall
       </i>
       ). There is also variation within Valencia, such as 'corn', which is
       <i>
        dacsa
       </i>
       in Central and Southern Valencian, but
       <i>
        panís
       </i>
       in Alicante and Northern Valencian (as well as in Northwestern Catalan). Since Standard Valencian is based on the Southern dialect, words from this dialect are often used as primary forms in the standard language, despite other words traditionally being used in other Valencian dialects. Examples of this are
       <i>
        tomaca
       </i>
       'tomato' (which is
       <i>
        tomata
       </i>
       outside of Southern Valencian) and
       <i>
        matalaf
       </i>
       'mattress' (which is
       <i>
        matalap
       </i>
       in most of Valencia, including parts of the Southern Valencian area).
      </p>
      <p>
       Below are a selection of words which differ or have different forms in Standard Valencian and Catalan. In many cases, both standards include this variation in their respective dictionaries, but differ as to what form is considered primary. In other cases, Valencian includes colloquial forms not present in the IEC standard. Primary forms in each standard are shown in bold (and may be more than one form). Words in brackets are present in the standard in question, but differ in meaning from how the
       <a href="/wiki/Cognate" title="Cognate">
        cognate
       </a>
       is used in the other standard.
      </p>

         </a>

         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29">

          </a>
         </sup>

      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Varieties_of_Valencian">
        Varieties of Valencian
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Valencian&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Varieties of Valencian">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Standard_Valencian">
        Standard Valencian
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Valencian&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Standard Valencian">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Acad%C3%A8mia_Valenciana_de_la_Llengua" title="Acadèmia Valenciana de la Llengua">
        Academy of Valencian Studies
       </a>
       (
       <i>
        Acadèmia Valenciana de la Llengua
       </i>
       , AVL), established by law in 1998 by the
       <a href="/wiki/Generalitat_Valenciana" title="Generalitat Valenciana">
        Valencian autonomous government
       </a>
       and constituted in 2001, is in charge of dictating the official rules governing the use of Valencian.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31">
        <a href="#cite_note-31">
         [30]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Currently, the majority of people who write in Valencian use this standard.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELledó2011339_32-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELledó2011339-32">
         [31]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Standard Valencian is based on the standard of the
       <a href="/wiki/Institut_d%27Estudis_Catalans" title="Institut d'Estudis Catalans">
        Institute of Catalan Studies
       </a>
       (
       <i>
        Institut d'Estudis Catalans
       </i>
       , IEC), used in
       <a href="/wiki/Catalonia" title="Catalonia">
        Catalonia
       </a>
       , with a few adaptations.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELledó2011338_33-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELledó2011338-33">
         [32]
        </a>
       </sup>
       This standard roughly follows the
       <a href="/wiki/Normes_de_Castell%C3%B3" title="Normes de Castelló">
        Rules of Castelló
       </a>
       (
       <i>
        Normes de Castelló
       </i>
       ) from 1932,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAcadèmia_Valenciana_de_la_Llengua2005_34-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAcadèmia_Valenciana_de_la_Llengua2005-34">
         [33]
        </a>
       </sup>
       a set of othographic guidelines regarded as a compromise between the essence and style of
       <a href="/wiki/Pompeu_Fabra" title="Pompeu Fabra">
        Pompeu Fabra
       </a>
       's guidelines, but also allowing the use of Valencian idiosyncrasies.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Valencian_subdialects">
        Valencian subdialects
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Valencian&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Valencian subdialects">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Subdialectes_del_valenci%C3%A0.svg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1090" data-file-width="643" height="339" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Subdialectes_del_valenci%C3%A0.svg/200px-Subdialectes_del_valenci%C3%A0.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Subdialectes_del_valenci%C3%A0.svg/300px-Subdialectes_del_valenci%C3%A0.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Subdialectes_del_valenci%C3%A0.svg/400px-Subdialectes_del_valenci%C3%A0.svg.png 2x" width="200"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Subdialectes_del_valenci%C3%A0.svg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Subdialects of Valencian
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <b>
         Transitional Valencian
        </b>
        (
        <i>
         valencià de transició
        </i>
        or
        <i>
         tortosí
        </i>
        ): spoken only in the northernmost areas of the province of
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Castell%C3%B3n_(province)" title="Castellón (province)">
         Castellón
        </a>
        in towns like
        <a href="/wiki/Benicarl%C3%B3" title="Benicarló">
         Benicarló
        </a>
        or
        <a href="/wiki/Vinar%C3%B2s" title="Vinaròs">
         Vinaròs
        </a>
        , the area of
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Matarranya" title="Matarranya">
         Matarranya
        </a>
        in
        <a href="/wiki/Aragon" title="Aragon">
         Aragon
        </a>
        (province of
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Teruel_(province)" title="Teruel (province)">
         Teruel
        </a>
        ), and a southern border area of
        <a href="/wiki/Catalonia" title="Catalonia">
         Catalonia
        </a>
        surrounding
        <a href="/wiki/Tortosa" title="Tortosa">
         Tortosa
        </a>
        , in the province of
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tarragona_(province)" title="Tarragona (province)">
         Tarragona
        </a>
        .
        <ul>
         <li>
          Word-initial and postconsonantal
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           /dʒ/
          </span>
          (Catalan
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           /ʒ/
          </span>
          and
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           /dʒ/~/ʒ/
          </span>
          ) alternates with
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           [(j)ʒ]
          </span>
          intervocalically; e.g.
          <i>
           joc
          </i>
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           [ˈdʒɒk]
          </span>
          'game', but
          <i>
           pitjor
          </i>
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           [piˈʒo]
          </span>
          'worse',
          <i>
           boja
          </i>
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           [ˈbɒjʒa]
          </span>
          'crazy' (Standard Valencian
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           /ˈdʒɔk/
          </span>
          ,
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           /piˈdʒoɾ/
          </span>
          ;
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           /ˈbɔdʒa/
          </span>
          ; Standard Catalan
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           /ˈʒɔk/
          </span>
          ,
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           /piˈdʒo/
          </span>
          and
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           /ˈbɔʒə/
          </span>
          ).
         </li>
         <li>
          Final ⟨r⟩
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           [
           <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alveolar_flap" title="Alveolar flap">
            ɾ
           </a>
           ]
          </span>
          isn't pronounced in infinitives; e.g.
          <i>
           cantar
          </i>
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           [kanˈta]
          </span>
          (instead of
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           /kanˈtaɾ/
          </span>
          ) 'to sing'.
         </li>
         <li>
          Archaic
          <a href="/wiki/Article_(grammar)" title="Article (grammar)">
           articles
          </a>
          <i>
           lo, los
          </i>
          ('the') are used instead of
          <i>
           el, els
          </i>
          ; e.g.
          <i>
           lo xic
          </i>
          'the boy',
          <i>
           los hòmens
          </i>
          'the men'.
         </li>
        </ul>
       </li>
       <li>
        <b>
         Northern Valencian
        </b>
        (
        <i>
         valencià septentrional
        </i>
        or
        <i>
         castellonenc
        </i>
        ): spoken in an area surrounding the city of
        <a href="/wiki/Castell%C3%B3n_de_la_Plana" title="Castellón de la Plana">
         Castellón de la Plana
        </a>
        .
        <ul>
         <li>
          Use of
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           [e]
          </span>
          sound instead of standard ⟨a⟩
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           /a/
          </span>
          in the third person singular of most verbs; e.g.
          <i>
           (ell) cantava
          </i>
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           [ˈkantave]
          </span>
          (instead of
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           /kanˈtava/
          </span>
          ) 'he sang'. Thus, Northern Valencian dialects contrast forms like
          <i>
           (jo) cantava
          </i>
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           [kanˈtava]
          </span>
          'I sang' with
          <i>
           (ell) cantava
          </i>
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           [kanˈtave]
          </span>
          'he sang', but merges
          <i>
           (jo) cante
          </i>
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           [ˈkante]
          </span>
          'I sing' with
          <i>
           (ell) canta
          </i>
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           [ˈkante]
          </span>
          'he sings'.
         </li>
         <li>
          Palatalization of ⟨ts⟩
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           /ts/ &gt; [tʃ]
          </span>
          and ⟨tz⟩
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           /dz/ &gt; [dʒ]
          </span>
          ; e.g.
          <i>
           pots
          </i>
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           /ˈpots/ &gt; [ˈpotʃ]
          </span>
          'cans, jars, you can',
          <i>
           dotze
          </i>
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           /ˈdodze/ &gt; [ˈdodʒe]
          </span>
          'twelve'.
         </li>
         <li>
          Depalatalization of
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           /ʃ/
          </span>
          to
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           [sʲ]
          </span>
          ; e.g.
          <i>
           caixa
          </i>
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           [ˈkajʃa] &gt; [ˈkajsʲa]
          </span>
          'box'.
         </li>
        </ul>
       </li>
       <li>
        <b>
         Central Valencian
        </b>
        (
        <i>
         valencià central
        </i>
        or
        <i>
         apitxat
        </i>
        ), spoken in
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Valencia,_Spain" title="Valencia, Spain">
         Valencia
        </a>
        city and its area, but not used as standard by the Valencian media.
        <ul>
         <li>
          Sibilant merger: all voiced sibilants are devoiced (
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           /dʒ/ &gt; [tʃ]
          </span>
          ,
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           /dz/ &gt; [ts]
          </span>
          ,
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           /z/ &gt; [s]
          </span>
          ); that is,
          <i>
           apitxat
          </i>
          pronounces
          <i>
           casa
          </i>
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           [ˈkasa]
          </span>
          ('house') and
          <i>
           joc
          </i>
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           [ˈtʃɒk]
          </span>
          ('game'), where other Valencians would pronounce
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           /ˈkaza/
          </span>
          and
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           /ˈdʒɔk/
          </span>
          (feature shared with
          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ribagor%C3%A7an" title="Ribagorçan">
           Ribagorçan
          </a>
          ).
         </li>
         <li>
          <a href="/wiki/Betacism" title="Betacism">
           Betacism
          </a>
          , that is the merge of
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           /v/
          </span>
          into
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           /b/
          </span>
          ; e.g.
          <i>
           viu
          </i>
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           [ˈbiw]
          </span>
          (instead of
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           /ˈviw/
          </span>
          ) 'he lives'.
         </li>
         <li>
          Fortition (gemination) and vocalisation of final consonants;
          <i>
           nit
          </i>
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           [ˈnitːë]
          </span>
          (instead of
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           /ˈnit/
          </span>
          ) 'night'.
         </li>
         <li>
          It preserves the strong simple past, which has been substituted by an analytic past (periphrastic past) with
          <span class="smallcaps" style="font-variant:small-caps;">
           vadere
          </span>
          +
          <a href="/wiki/Infinitive" title="Infinitive">
           infinitive
          </a>
          in the rest of modern Catalan and Valencian variants. For example,
          <i>
           aní
          </i>
          instead of
          <i>
           vaig anar
          </i>
          'I went'.
         </li>
        </ul>
       </li>
       <li>
        <b>
         Southern Valencian
        </b>
        (
        <i>
         valencià meridional
        </i>
        ): spoken in the contiguous
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Comarques_of_the_Valencian_Community" title="Comarques of the Valencian Community">
          comarques
         </a>
        </i>
        located in the southernmost part of the Valencia province and the northernmost part in the province of Alicante. This subdialect is considered as Standard Valencian.
        <ul>
         <li>
          <a href="/wiki/Vowel_harmony" title="Vowel harmony">
           Vowel harmony
          </a>
          : the final syllable of a disyllabic word adopts a preceding open ⟨e⟩
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           [æ]
          </span>
          or ⟨o⟩
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           [ɒ]
          </span>
          if the final vowel is an unstressed -⟨a⟩ or -⟨e⟩; e.g.
          <i>
           terra
          </i>
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           [ˈtæræ]
          </span>
          ('earth, land'),
          <i>
           dona
          </i>
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           [ˈdɒnɒ]
          </span>
          ('woman').
         </li>
         <li>
          This subdialect retain geminate consonants (⟨tl⟩
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           /lː/
          </span>
          and ⟨tn⟩
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           /nː/
          </span>
          ); e.g.
          <i>
           guatla
          </i>
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           [ˈɡwalːa]
          </span>
          'quail',
          <i>
           cotna
          </i>
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           [ˈkonːa]
          </span>
          'rind'.
         </li>
         <li>
          Weak pronouns are "reinforced" in front of the verb (
          <i>
           em, en, et, es
          </i>
          , etc.) contrary to other subdialects which maintains "full form" (
          <i>
           me, ne, te, se
          </i>
          , etc.).
         </li>
        </ul>
       </li>
       <li>
        <b>
         Alicante Valencian
        </b>
        (
        <i>
         valencià alacantí
        </i>
        ): spoken in the southern half of the province of
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alicante_(province)" title="Alicante (province)">
         Alicante
        </a>
        , and the area of
        <a href="/wiki/Carche" title="Carche">
         Carche
        </a>
        in
        <a href="/wiki/Region_of_Murcia" title="Region of Murcia">
         Murcia
        </a>
        .
        <ul>
         <li>
          Intervocalic
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           /d/
          </span>
          elision in most instances; e.g.
          <i>
           roda
          </i>
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           [ˈrɒa]
          </span>
          'wheel',
          <i>
           nadal
          </i>
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           [naˈal]
          </span>
          'Christmas'.
         </li>
         <li>
          Yod is not pronounced in ⟨ix⟩
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           /jʃ/ &gt; [ʃ]
          </span>
          ; e.g.
          <i>
           caixa
          </i>
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           [ˈkaʃa]
          </span>
          'box'.
         </li>
         <li>
          Final ⟨r⟩ isn't pronounced in infinitives; e.g.
          <i>
           cantar
          </i>
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           [kanˈta]
          </span>
          'to sing'.
         </li>
         <li>
          There are some archaisms like:
          <i>
           ans
          </i>
          instead of
          <i>
           abans
          </i>
          'before',
          <i>
           manco
          </i>
          instead of
          <i>
           menys
          </i>
          'less',
          <i>
           dintre
          </i>
          instead of
          <i>
           dins
          </i>
          'into' or
          <i>
           devers
          </i>
          instead of
          <i>
           cap a
          </i>
          'towards'.
         </li>
         <li>
          There are more interferences with Spanish than other dialects:
          <i>
           assul
          </i>
          (from
          <i>
           azul
          </i>
          ) instead of
          <i>
           blau
          </i>
          (or
          <i>
           atzur
          </i>
          ) 'blue',
          <i>
           llimpiar
          </i>
          (from
          <i>
           limpiar
          </i>
          ) instead of
          <i>
           netejar
          </i>
          'to clean' or
          <i>
           sacar
          </i>
          (from
          <i>
           sacar
          </i>
          ) instead of
          <i>
           traure
          </i>
          'take out'.
         </li>
        </ul>
       </li>
      </ul>

      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Middle_Ages">
        Middle Ages
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Valencian&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Middle Ages">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <i>
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Misteri_d%27Elx" title="Misteri d'Elx">
          Misteri d'Elx
         </a>
        </i>
        (c. 1350). Liturgical drama. Listed as
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Masterpiece_of_the_Oral_and_Intangible_Heritage_of_Humanity" title="Masterpiece of the Oral and Intangible Heritage of Humanity">
         Masterpiece of the Oral and Intangible Heritage of Humanity
        </a>
        by
        <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">
         UNESCO
        </a>
        .
       </li>
      </ul>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Renaissance">
        Renaissance
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Valencian&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Renaissance">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Ausi%C3%A0s_March" title="Ausiàs March">
         Ausiàs March
        </a>
        (Gandia, 1400 – Valencia, 3 March 1459). Poet, widely read in renaissance Europe.
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Joanot_Martorell" title="Joanot Martorell">
         Joanot Martorell
        </a>
        (Gandia, 1413–1468). Knight and the author of the novel
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Tirant_lo_Blanch" title="Tirant lo Blanch">
          Tirant lo Blanch
         </a>
        </i>
        .
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Isabel_de_Villena" title="Isabel de Villena">
         Isabel de Villena
        </a>
        (Valencia, 1430–1490). Religious poet.
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Joan_Ro%C3%ADs_de_Corella" title="Joan Roís de Corella">
         Joan Roís de Corella
        </a>
        (Gandia or Valencia, 1435 – Valencia, 1497). Knight and poet.
       </li>
       <li>
        <i>
         <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Obres_e_trobes_en_lahors_de_la_Verge_Maria&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Obres e trobes en lahors de la Verge Maria (page does not exist)">
          Obres e trobes en lahors de la Verge Maria
         </a>
        </i>
        (1474) The first book printed in Spain. It is the compendium of a religious poetry contest held that year in the town of Valencia.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECosta_CarrerasYates20096–7_12-1">
         <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECosta_CarrerasYates20096–7-12">
          [11]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
      </ul>

       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:RTVVexecutada.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1944" data-file-width="2592" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/RTVVexecutada.jpg/220px-RTVVexecutada.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/RTVVexecutada.jpg/330px-RTVVexecutada.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/RTVVexecutada.jpg/440px-RTVVexecutada.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:RTVVexecutada.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Employees demonstrate in front of the RTVV headquarters in
         <a href="/wiki/Burjassot" title="Burjassot">
          Burjassot
         </a>
         the day of its closure
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Until its dissolution in November 2013, the public-service Ràdio Televisió Valenciana (RTVV) was the main broadcaster of radio and television in Valencian language. The Generalitat Valenciana constituted it in 1984 in order to guarantee the
       <a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_information" title="Freedom of information">
        freedom of information
       </a>
       of the Valencian people in their own language.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35">
        <a href="#cite_note-35">
         [34]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Prior to its dissolution, the administration of RTVV under the
       <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Party_(Spain)" title="People's Party (Spain)">
        People's Party
       </a>
       (PP) had been controversial due to accusations of ideological manipulation and lack of plurality. The news broadcast was accused of giving marginal coverage of the
       <a href="/wiki/Valencia_Metro_derailment" title="Valencia Metro derailment">
        Valencia Metro derailment
       </a>
       in 2006 and the indictment of President de la Generalitat
       <a href="/wiki/Francisco_Camps" title="Francisco Camps">
        Francisco Camps
       </a>
       in the
       <a href="/wiki/G%C3%BCrtel_case" title="Gürtel case">
        Gürtel
       </a>
       scandal in 2009.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36">
        <a href="#cite_note-36">
         [35]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Supervisors appointed by the PP were accused of
       <a href="/wiki/Sexual_harassment" title="Sexual harassment">
        sexual harassment
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37">
        <a href="#cite_note-37">
         [36]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In face of an increasing debt due to excessive expenditure by the PP, RTVV announced in 2012 a plan to shed 70% of its labour. The plan was nullified on 5 November 2013 by the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Court_of_Spain" title="National Court of Spain">
        National Court
       </a>
       after trade unions appealed against it. On that same day, the President de la Generalitat
       <a href="/wiki/Alberto_Fabra" title="Alberto Fabra">
        Alberto Fabra
       </a>
       (also from
       <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Party_(Spain)" title="People's Party (Spain)">
        PP
       </a>
       ) announced RTVV would be closed, claiming that reinstating the employees was untenable.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38">
        <a href="#cite_note-38">
         [37]
        </a>
       </sup>
       On 27 November, the legislative assembly passed the dissolution of RTVV and employees organized to take control of the broadcast, starting a campaign against the PP. Nou TV's last broadcast ended abruptly when Spanish police pulled the plug at 12:19 on 29 November 2013.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39">
        <a href="#cite_note-39">
         [38]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Having lost all revenues from advertisements and facing high costs from the termination of hundreds of contracts, critics question whether the closure of RTVV has improved the financial situation of the Generalitat, and point out to plans to benefit private-owned media.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40">
        <a href="#cite_note-40">
         [39]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Currently, the availability of media in the Valencian language is extremely limited. All the other
       <a href="/wiki/Autonomous_communities_of_Spain" title="Autonomous communities of Spain">
        autonomous communities in Spain
       </a>
       , including the monolingual ones, have public-service broadcasters, with the Valencian Community being the only exception despite being the fourth most populated.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Linguistic_controversy">
        Linguistic controversy
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Valencian&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Linguistic controversy">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Further information:
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Valencian_language_controversy" title="Valencian language controversy">
        Valencian language controversy
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Language_secessionism" title="Language secessionism">
        Language secessionism
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Blaverism" title="Blaverism">
        Blaverism
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Anti-Catalanism" title="Anti-Catalanism">
        Anti-Catalanism
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       Linguists, including Valencian scholars, deal with Catalan and Valencian as the same language. The official regulating body of the language of the Valencian community, the
       <a href="/wiki/Acad%C3%A8mia_Valenciana_de_la_Llengua" title="Acadèmia Valenciana de la Llengua">
        Valencian Language Academy
       </a>
       (
       <i>
        Acadèmia Valenciana de la Llengua,
       </i>
       AVL) considers Valencian and Catalan to be two names for the same language.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dictalmen_AVL_41-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-dictalmen_AVL-41">
         [40]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <table class="mbox-small plainlinks sistersitebox" role="presentation" style="background-color:#f9f9f9;border:1px solid #aaa;color:#000">
       <tr>
        <td class="mbox-image">
         <img alt="" class="noviewer" data-file-height="430" data-file-width="410" height="40" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Wikisource-logo.svg/38px-Wikisource-logo.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Wikisource-logo.svg/57px-Wikisource-logo.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Wikisource-logo.svg/76px-Wikisource-logo.svg.png 2x" width="38"/>
        </td>
        <td class="mbox-text plainlist">
         Catalan
         <a href="/wiki/Wikisource" title="Wikisource">
          Wikisource
         </a>
         has original text related to this article:
         <div style="margin-left: 10px;">
          <b>
           <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wikisource.org/wiki/ca:Dictamen_sobre_els_principis_i_criteris_per_a_la_defensa_de_la_denominaci%C3%B3_i_l%27entitat_del_valenci%C3%A0" title="s:ca:Dictamen sobre els principis i criteris per a la defensa de la denominació i l'entitat del valencià">
            AVL: Dictamen sobre els principis i criteris per a la defensa de la denominació i l'entitat del valencià
           </a>
          </b>
         </div>
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <blockquote class="templatequote">
       <p>
        [T]he historical patrimonial language of the
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Valencian_people" title="Valencian people">
         Valencian people
        </a>
        , from a philological standpoint, is the same shared by the autonomous communinites of
        <a href="/wiki/Catalonia" title="Catalonia">
         Catalonia
        </a>
        and
        <a href="/wiki/Balearic_Islands" title="Balearic Islands">
         Balearic islands
        </a>
        , and
        <a href="/wiki/Andorra" title="Andorra">
         Principality of Andorra
        </a>
        . Additionally, it is the patrimonial historical language of other territories of the ancient
        <a href="/wiki/Crown_of_Aragon" title="Crown of Aragon">
         Crown of Aragon
        </a>
        [...] The different varieties of these territories constitute a language, that is, a "linguistic system" [...] From this group of varieties, Valencian has the same hierarchy and dignity as any other dialectal modality of that linguistic system [...]
       </p>
       <div class="templatequotecite">
        —
        <cite>
         Ruling of the Valencian Language Academy of 9 February 2005, extract of point 1.
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAcadèmia_Valenciana_de_la_Llengua2005_34-1">
          <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAcadèmia_Valenciana_de_la_Llengua2005-34">
           [33]
          </a>
         </sup>
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42">
          <a href="#cite_note-42">
           [41]
          </a>
         </sup>
        </cite>
       </div>
      </blockquote>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Linguistic_map_Southwestern_Europe.gif">
         <img alt="Linguistic map Southwestern Europe.gif" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="544" data-file-width="600" height="272" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Linguistic_map_Southwestern_Europe.gif/300px-Linguistic_map_Southwestern_Europe.gif" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Linguistic_map_Southwestern_Europe.gif/450px-Linguistic_map_Southwestern_Europe.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/4/4d/Linguistic_map_Southwestern_Europe.gif 2x" width="300"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Linguistic_map_Southwestern_Europe.gif" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The AVL was established in 1998 by the PP-
       <a href="/wiki/Valencian_Union" title="Valencian Union">
        UV
       </a>
       government of
       <a href="/wiki/Eduardo_Zaplana" title="Eduardo Zaplana">
        Eduardo Zaplana
       </a>
       . According to
       <a href="/wiki/El_Pa%C3%ADs" title="El País">
        El País
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Jordi_Pujol" title="Jordi Pujol">
        Jordi Pujol
       </a>
       , then president of Catalonia and of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/CiU" title="CiU">
        CiU
       </a>
       , negotiated with Zaplana in 1996 to ensure the linguistic unity of Catalan in exchange for CiU support of the appointment of
       <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Mar%C3%ADa_Aznar" title="José María Aznar">
        José María Aznar
       </a>
       as
       <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Spain" title="Prime Minister of Spain">
        Prime Minister of Spain
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43">
        <a href="#cite_note-43">
         [42]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Zaplana has denied this, claiming that "[n]ever, never, was I able to negotiate that which is not negotiable, neither that which is not in the negotiating scope of a politician. That is, the unity of the language".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44">
        <a href="#cite_note-44">
         [b]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The AVL orthography is based on the
       <a href="/wiki/Normes_de_Castell%C3%B3" title="Normes de Castelló">
        Normes de Castelló
       </a>
       , a set of rules for writing Valencian established in 1932. A rival set of rules, called
       <i>
        Normes del Puig
       </i>
       , were established in 1979 by the association RACV (Real Acadèmia de Cultura Valenciana), which considers itself a rival language academy to the AVL, and promotes an alternative orthography. Compared to Standard Valencian, this orthography excludes many words not traditionally used in the Valencian Country, and also prefers spellings such as ⟨ch⟩ for /tʃ/ and ⟨y⟩ for /j/ (as in
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">
        Castilian
       </a>
       ). It is mainly used by private individuals. The position of the RACV is supported by a minority of Valencian scholars active in fields other than linguistics.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45">
        <a href="#cite_note-45">
         [43]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Valencian is classified as a Western dialect, along with the North-Western varieties spoken in Western Catalonia (
       <a href="/wiki/Province_of_Lleida" title="Province of Lleida">
        Province of Lleida
       </a>
       and most of the
       <a href="/wiki/Province_of_Tarragona" title="Province of Tarragona">
        Province of Tarragona
       </a>
       ).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFeldhausen20105_46-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFeldhausen20105-46">
         [44]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWheeler20052–3_47-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWheeler20052–3-47">
         [45]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The various forms of Catalan and Valencian are mutually intelligible (ranging from 90% to 95%)
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ethnologue_48-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-ethnologue-48">
         [46]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Despite the position of the official organizations, an opinion poll carried out between 2001 and 2004
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lavanguardia.mobi_9-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-lavanguardia.mobi-9">
         [8]
        </a>
       </sup>
       showed that the majority (65%) of the Valencian people (both Valencian and Spanish speakers) consider Valencian different from Catalan. This position is promoted by people who do not use Valencian regularly.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWheeler2003207_49-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWheeler2003207-49">
         [47]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Furthermore, the data indicates that younger generations educated in Valencian are much less likely to hold these views. According to an official poll made in 2014,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50">
        <a href="#cite_note-50">
         [48]
        </a>
       </sup>
       52% of Valencians considered Valencian to be a language different from Catalan, while 41% considered the languages to be the same. Also this poll showed significant differences regarding age and level of education, with a majority of those aged 18–24 (51%) and those with a higher education (58%) considering Valencian the same language as Catalan. This can be compared to those aged 65 and above (29%) and those with only primary education (32%), where the same view has its lowest support.
      </p>
      <p>
       The confusion regarding the term Valencian and its relation to Catalan has sometimes lead to confusion and controversy. In 2004, during the drafting of the
       <a href="/wiki/Treaty_establishing_a_Constitution_for_Europe" title="Treaty establishing a Constitution for Europe">
        European Constitution
       </a>
       , the regional governments of Spain where a language other than Spanish is co-official were asked to submit translations into the relevant language in question. Since different names are used in Catalonia ("Catalan") and in the Valencian Community ("Valencian"), the two regions provided one version each, both of which were identical to each other.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51">
        <a href="#cite_note-51">
         [49]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>

         <li id="cite_note-dictalmen_AVL-41">
          <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
           <b>
            <a href="#cite_ref-dictalmen_AVL_41-0">
             ^
            </a>
           </b>
          </span>
          <span class="reference-text">
           <a class="external text" href="http://ca.wikisource.org/wiki/Dictamen_sobre_els_principis_i_criteris_per_a_la_defensa_de_la_denominaci%C3%B3_i_l%27entitat_del_valenci%C3%A0">
            <i>
             "Dictamen de l'Acadèmia Valenciana de la Llengua sobre els principis i criteris per a la defensa de la denominació i l'entitat del valencià"
            </i>
           </a>
           . Report from
           <a href="/wiki/Acad%C3%A8mia_Valenciana_de_la_Llengua" title="Acadèmia Valenciana de la Llengua">
            Acadèmia Valenciana de la Llengua
           </a>
           about denomination and identity of Valencian.
          </span>
         </li>
         <li id="cite_note-42">
          <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
           <b>
            <a href="#cite_ref-42">
             ^
            </a>
           </b>
          </span>
          <span class="reference-text">
           Original full text of Dictamen 1:
           <i>
            D’acord amb les aportacions més solvents de la romanística acumulades des del segle XIX fins a l’actualitat (estudis de gramàtica històrica, de dialectologia, de sintaxi, de lexicografia…), la llengua pròpia i històrica dels valencians, des del punt de vista de la filologia, és també la que compartixen les comunitats autònomes de Catalunya i de les Illes Balears i el Principat d’Andorra. Així mateix és la llengua històrica i pròpia d’altres territoris de l’antiga Corona d’Aragó (la franja oriental aragonesa, la ciutat sarda de l’Alguer i el departament francés dels Pirineus Orientals). Els diferents parlars de tots estos territoris constituïxen una llengua, és a dir, un mateix "sistema lingüístic", segons la terminologia del primer estructuralisme (annex 1) represa en el Dictamen del Consell Valencià de Cultura, que figura com a preàmbul de la Llei de Creació de l’AVL. Dins d’eixe conjunt de parlars, el valencià té la mateixa jerarquia i dignitat que qualsevol altra modalitat territorial del sistema lingüístic, i presenta unes característiques pròpies que l’AVL preservarà i potenciarà d’acord amb la tradició lexicogràfica i literària pròpia, la realitat lingüística valenciana i la normativització consolidada a partir de les Normes de Castelló.
           </i>
          </span>
         </li>

                <div class="hlist hlist-separated">
                 <ul>
                  <li>
                   <i>
                    Italics
                   </i>
                   indicate
                   <a href="/wiki/Language_death" title="Language death">
                    extinct languages
                   </a>
                  </li>
                  <li>
                   <b>
                    Bold
                   </b>
                   indicates
                   <a href="/wiki/List_of_languages_by_number_of_native_speakers" title="List of languages by number of native speakers">
                    languages with more than 5 million speakers
                   </a>
                  </li>
                  <li>
                   Languages between parentheses are
                   <a href="/wiki/Variety_(linguistics)" title="Variety (linguistics)">
                    varieties
                   </a>
                   of the language on their left.
                  </li>
                 </ul>
                </div>
               </div>
              </td>
             </tr>
            </table>
           </div>
